<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Henry's law</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>

<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Relation of equilibrium solubility of a gas in a liquid to its partial pressure in the contacting gas phase </div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-multiple_issues compact-ambox" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span"><div class="mw-collapsible" style="width:95%; margin: 0.2em 0;"><b>This article has multiple issues.</b> Please help <b><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit">improve it</a></b> or discuss these issues on the <b><a href="/wiki/Talk:Henry%27s_law" title="Talk:Henry's law">talk page</a></b>. <small><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove these template messages</a>)</i></small>

</div><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>, <b>Henry's law</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Gas_laws" title="Gas laws">gas law</a> that states that the amount of dissolved gas is proportional to its partial pressure in the gas phase. The proportionality factor is called the Henry's law constant. It was formulated by the English chemist <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_(chemist)" title="William Henry (chemist)">William Henry</a>, who studied the topic in the early 19th century. In his publication about the quantity of gases absorbed by water,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Henry1803_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Henry1803-1">[1]</a></sup> he described the results of his experiments:
</p>
<dl><dd><i>..."water takes up, of gas condensed by one, two, or more additional atmospheres, a quantity which, ordinarily compressed, would be equal to twice, thrice, &amp;c. the volume absorbed under the common pressure of the atmosphere."</i></dd></dl>
<p>An example where Henry's law is at play is in the depth-dependent dissolution of oxygen and nitrogen in the blood of <a href="/wiki/Underwater_diving" title="Underwater diving">underwater divers</a> that changes during <a href="/wiki/Decompression_(diving)" title="Decompression (diving)">decompression</a>, leading to <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness" title="Decompression sickness">decompression sickness</a>. An everyday example is given by one's experience with <a href="/wiki/Carbonation" title="Carbonation">carbonated</a> <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drinks</a>, which contain dissolved carbon dioxide. Before opening, the gas above the drink in its container is almost pure <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>, at a pressure higher than <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">atmospheric pressure</a>. After the bottle is opened, this gas escapes, moving the partial pressure of carbon dioxide above the liquid to be much lower, resulting in degassing as the dissolved carbon dioxide comes out of solution.
</p>

<h2><span id="Fundamental_types_and_variants_of_Henry.27s_law_constants"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Fundamental_types_and_variants_of_Henry's_law_constants">Fundamental types and variants of Henry's law constants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Fundamental types and variants of Henry's law constants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(March 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>There are many ways to define the proportionality constant of Henry's law, which can be subdivided into two fundamental types: One possibility is to put the aqueous phase into the numerator and the gaseous phase into the denominator ("aq/gas").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sander2015_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sander2015-2">[2]</a></sup> This results in the Henry's law solubility constant <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>H</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/75a9edddcca2f782014371f75dca39d7e13a9c1b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.064ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>. Its value increases with increased solubility. Alternatively, numerator and denominator can be switched ("gas/aq"), which results in the Henry's law volatility constant <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle K_{\rm {H}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>K</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">H</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle K_{\rm {H}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="K_{\rm H}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8ea835431ce9701b861e9a57aee5652698fd99f7" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.438ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>. The value of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle K_{\rm {H}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>K</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">H</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle K_{\rm {H}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="K_{\rm H}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8ea835431ce9701b861e9a57aee5652698fd99f7" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.438ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> decreases with increased solubility. There are several variants of both fundamental types. This results from the multiplicity of quantities that can be chosen to describe the composition of the two phases. Typical choices for the aqueous phase are <a href="/wiki/Molar_concentration" title="Molar concentration">molar concentration</a> (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c_{\rm {a}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c_{\rm {a}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="c_{\rm a}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1da615d66f209eaf9a539b55583810b8d4051116" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.061ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span>), <a href="/wiki/Molality" title="Molality">molality</a> (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>b</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f11423fbb2e967f986e36804a8ae4271734917c3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.998ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>), and molar <a href="/wiki/Mixing_ratio" title="Mixing ratio">mixing ratio</a> (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>). For the gas phase, molar concentration (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c_{\rm {g}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c_{\rm {g}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="c_{\rm g}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6fbdb09ea6ffbaa52de83aa762be418abad6f448" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.061ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>) and <a href="/wiki/Partial_pressure" title="Partial pressure">partial pressure</a> (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle p}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>p</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle p}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="p" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81eac1e205430d1f40810df36a0edffdc367af36" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:1.259ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span>) are often used. It is not possible to use the gas-phase mixing ratio (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle y}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>y</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="y" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b8a6208ec717213d4317e666f1ae872e00620a0d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.155ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span>) because at a given gas-phase mixing ratio, the aqueous-phase concentration <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c_{\rm {a}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c_{\rm {a}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="c_{\rm a}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1da615d66f209eaf9a539b55583810b8d4051116" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.061ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> depends on the total pressure and thus the ratio <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle y/c_{\rm {a}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>y</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y/c_{\rm {a}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="y/c_{\rm a}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/466a2dfdac309ab0ebdb43797d04116de935c4a3" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.379ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> is not a constant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sander1999_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sander1999-3">[3]</a></sup> To specify the exact variant of the Henry's law constant, two superscripts are used. They refer to the numerator and the denominator of the definition. For example, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{cp}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>c</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{cp}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H^{cp}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3484e43d53b6be7b4bf4893996e003747b9695e1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.875ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> refers to the Henry solubility defined as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c/p}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>p</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c/p}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="c/p" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b1595225d0ae0277dc2282288bf98bc28afe3c3e" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:3.339ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Henry.27s_law_solubility_constants_.7F.27.22.60UNIQ--postMath-0000000E-QINU.60.22.27.7F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Henry's_law_solubility_constants_'&quot;`UNIQ--postMath-0000000E-QINU`&quot;'">Henry's law solubility constants <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>H</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/75a9edddcca2f782014371f75dca39d7e13a9c1b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.064ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Henry's law solubility constants  $H">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h4><span id="Henry_solubility_defined_via_concentration_.28.7F.27.22.60UNIQ--postMath-0000000F-QINU.60.22.27.7F.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Henry_solubility_defined_via_concentration_('&quot;`UNIQ--postMath-0000000F-QINU`&quot;')">Henry solubility defined via concentration (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{cp}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>c</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{cp}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H^{cp}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3484e43d53b6be7b4bf4893996e003747b9695e1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.875ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Henry solubility defined via concentration ( $H^{cp})">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Atmospheric chemists often define the Henry solubility as
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{cp}=c_{\text{a}}/p}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>c</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>a</mtext>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>p</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{cp}=c_{\text{a}}/p}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle H^{cp}=c_{\text{a}}/p}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/378dafee02db35f4078c54ccdfef3bded7790082" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.366ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sander2015_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sander2015-2">[2]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Here <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c_{\text{a}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>a</mtext>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c_{\text{a}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle c_{\text{a}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/77b40f78deeab992bc10c160d377eb0430c0fec7" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.061ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is the concentration of a species in the aqueous phase, and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle p}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>p</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle p}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="p" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81eac1e205430d1f40810df36a0edffdc367af36" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:1.259ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is the partial pressure of that species in the gas phase under equilibrium conditions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SI_unit" title="SI unit">SI unit</a> for <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{cp}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{cp}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H^{cp}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3484e43d53b6be7b4bf4893996e003747b9695e1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.875ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> is mol/(m<sup>3</sup> Pa); however, often the unit M/atm is used, since <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c_{\text{a}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c_{\text{a}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle c_{\text{a}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/77b40f78deeab992bc10c160d377eb0430c0fec7" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.061ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is usually expressed in M (1 M = 1 mol/dm<sup>3</sup>) and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle p}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="p" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81eac1e205430d1f40810df36a0edffdc367af36" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:1.259ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> in atm (1 atm = 101325 Pa).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. </p>
<h4><span id="The_dimensionless_Henry_solubility_.7F.27.22.60UNIQ--postMath-00000016-QINU.60.22.27.7F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_dimensionless_Henry_solubility_'&quot;`UNIQ--postMath-00000016-QINU`&quot;'">The dimensionless Henry solubility <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{cc}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>c</mi>
<mi>c</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{cc}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H^{cc}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3ff585731c5c66c4662e2d29fc638ca0c1b3ab6a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.76ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The dimensionless Henry solubility  $H^{cc}">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Henry solubility can also be expressed as the dimensionless ratio between the aqueous-phase concentration <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c_{\text{a}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>a</mtext>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c_{\text{a}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle c_{\text{a}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/77b40f78deeab992bc10c160d377eb0430c0fec7" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.061ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> of a species and its gas-phase concentration <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c_{\text{g}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>g</mtext>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c_{\text{g}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle c_{\text{g}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a3dc4bfac07a0d2ca9f84d81845157fcdd6d8029" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.061ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{cc}=c_{\text{a}}/c_{\text{g}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

<mi>c</mi>
<mi>c</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>a</mtext>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</mrow>
<msub>

</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{cc}=c_{\text{a}}/c_{\text{g}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle H^{cc}=c_{\text{a}}/c_{\text{g}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f0fa46e09f9b1f16eceba46d2552a6dc0efc2d40" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:12.143ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sander2015_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sander2015-2">[2]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>For an ideal gas, the conversion is:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{cc}=H^{cp}\times RT}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>c</mi>
<mi>c</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>c</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
<mi>R</mi>
<mi>T</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{cc}=H^{cp}\times RT}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle H^{cc}=H^{cp}\times RT}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/09cc8db5f701c37554c8294f04b4c655c3a92f8f" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:16.973ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> ,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sander2015_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sander2015-2">[2]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle R}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>R</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle R}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="R" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4b0bfb3769bf24d80e15374dc37b0441e2616e33" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.764ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Gas_constant" title="Gas constant">gas constant</a> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle T}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>T</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle T}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="T" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ec7200acd984a1d3a3d7dc455e262fbe54f7f6e0" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.636ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is the temperature.
</p><p>Sometimes, this dimensionless constant is called the "water-air partitioning coefficient" <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle K_{\text{WA}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>K</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>WA</mtext>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle K_{\text{WA}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle K_{\text{WA}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5bea2091474636ce788e7ef2cf01e349c29ca370" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:5.127ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> It is closely related to the various, slightly different definitions of the "Ostwald coefficient" <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle L}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h4><span id="Henry_solubility_defined_via_aqueous-phase_mixing_ratio_.28.7F.27.22.60UNIQ--postMath-0000001F-QINU.60.22.27.7F.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Henry_solubility_defined_via_aqueous-phase_mixing_ratio_('&quot;`UNIQ--postMath-0000001F-QINU`&quot;')">Henry solubility defined via aqueous-phase mixing ratio (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{xp}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>x</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{xp}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H^{xp}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c58493c378ac8d7e5923ba0151d852bd83174a53" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:4.103ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Henry solubility defined via aqueous-phase mixing ratio ( $H^{xp})">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Another Henry's law solubility constant is
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{xp}=x/p}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>x</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>p</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{xp}=x/p}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle H^{xp}=x/p}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f893ece9b508c8a1f10f2232fce375fe28069d71" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.863ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sander2015_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-Sander2015-2">[2]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Here <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

For a dilute aqueous solution the conversion between <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<h4><span id="Henry_solubility_defined_via_molality_.28.7F.27.22.60UNIQ--postMath-00000029-QINU.60.22.27.7F.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Henry_solubility_defined_via_molality_('&quot;`UNIQ--postMath-00000029-QINU`&quot;')">Henry solubility defined via molality (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{bp}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>b</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{bp}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H^{bp}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/49e49ca29268d03fec2a70d62eeca7f1e42acba1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.868ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Henry solubility defined via molality ( $H^{bp})">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(March 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>It can be advantageous to describe the aqueous phase in terms of molality instead of concentration. The molality of a solution does not change with <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle T}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>T</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle T}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="T" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ec7200acd984a1d3a3d7dc455e262fbe54f7f6e0" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.636ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, since it refers to the <i>mass</i> of the solvent. In contrast, the concentration <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>c</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86a67b81c2de995bd608d5b2df50cd8cd7d92455" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.007ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> does change with <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle T}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>T</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle T}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="T" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ec7200acd984a1d3a3d7dc455e262fbe54f7f6e0" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.636ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, since the density of a solution and thus its volume are temperature-dependent. Defining the aqueous-phase composition via molality has the advantage that any temperature dependence of the Henry's law constant is a true solubility phenomenon and not introduced indirectly via a density change of the solution. Using molality, the Henry solubility can be defined as
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{bp}=b/p.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>b</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>p</mi>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{bp}=b/p.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H^{bp} = b / p." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e7ae242f975be88dc8f5d395c8d5f12f77586459" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.943ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Here <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>b</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f11423fbb2e967f986e36804a8ae4271734917c3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.998ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is used as the symbol for molality (instead of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle m}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>m</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle m}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="m" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a07d98bb302f3856cbabc47b2b9016692e3f7bc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.04ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>) to avoid confusion with the symbol <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle m}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>m</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle m}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="m" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a07d98bb302f3856cbabc47b2b9016692e3f7bc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.04ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> for mass. The SI unit for <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{bp}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>b</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{bp}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H^{bp}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/49e49ca29268d03fec2a70d62eeca7f1e42acba1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.868ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> is mol/(kg Pa). There is no simple way to calculate <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{cp}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>c</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{cp}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H^{cp}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3484e43d53b6be7b4bf4893996e003747b9695e1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.875ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> from <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{bp}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>b</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{bp}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H^{bp}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/49e49ca29268d03fec2a70d62eeca7f1e42acba1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.868ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>, since the conversion between concentration <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c_{\text{a}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>a</mtext>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c_{\text{a}}}</annotation>
</semantics>

<h4><span id="The_Bunsen_coefficient_.7F.27.22.60UNIQ--postMath-00000042-QINU.60.22.27.7F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bunsen_coefficient_'&quot;`UNIQ--postMath-00000042-QINU`&quot;'">The Bunsen coefficient <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \alpha }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>α<!-- α --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \alpha }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\alpha " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b79333175c8b3f0840bfb4ec41b8072c83ea88d3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.488ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The Bunsen coefficient  $\alpha ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>According to Sazonov and Shaw, the dimensionless Bunsen coefficient <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \alpha }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>α<!-- α --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \alpha }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\alpha " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b79333175c8b3f0840bfb4ec41b8072c83ea88d3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.488ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is defined as "the volume of saturating gas, V1, reduced to T° = 273.15 K, p° = 1 bar, which is absorbed by unit volume V<sub>2</sub>* of pure solvent at the temperature of measurement and partial pressure of 1 bar."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SazonovShaw2006_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-SazonovShaw2006-6">[6]</a></sup> If the gas is ideal, the pressure cancels out, and the conversion to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{cp}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>c</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{cp}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H^{cp}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3484e43d53b6be7b4bf4893996e003747b9695e1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.875ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> is simply
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{cp}=\alpha \times {\frac {1}{RT^{\text{STP}}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>c</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>α<!-- α --></mi>
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mn>1</mn>
<mrow>
<mi>R</mi>
<msup>
<mi>T</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>STP</mtext>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{cp}=\alpha \times {\frac {1}{RT^{\text{STP}}}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle H^{cp}=\alpha \times {\frac {1}{RT^{\text{STP}}}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f3641869dd3663b8b5058a583ff15e6a8ba7660e" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:19.073ex; height:5.509ex;"/></span> ,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (March 2016)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup></dd></dl>
<p>with <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle T^{\text{STP}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>T</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>STP</mtext>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle T^{\text{STP}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle T^{\text{STP}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/085b38507210c8dcf249a995fd9ced532558ada5" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.172ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> = 273.15 K. Note, that according to this definition, the conversion factor is <i>not</i> temperature-dependent.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Independent of the temperature that the Bunsen coefficient refers to, 273.15 K is always used for the conversion.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Bunsen coefficient, which is named after <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bunsen" title="Robert Bunsen">Robert Bunsen</a>, has been used mainly in the older literature.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="The_Kuenen_coefficient_.7F.27.22.60UNIQ--postMath-00000047-QINU.60.22.27.7F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Kuenen_coefficient_'&quot;`UNIQ--postMath-00000047-QINU`&quot;'">The Kuenen coefficient <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle S}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>S</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="S" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The Kuenen coefficient  $S">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>According to Sazonov and Shaw, the Kuenen coefficient <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle S}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>S</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="S" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is defined as "the volume of saturating gas V(g), reduced to T° = 273.15 K, p° = bar, which is dissolved by unit mass of pure solvent at the temperature of measurement and partial pressure 1 bar."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SazonovShaw2006_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-SazonovShaw2006-6">[6]</a></sup> If the gas is ideal, the relation to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{cp}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>H</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>c</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{cp}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="H^{cp}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3484e43d53b6be7b4bf4893996e003747b9695e1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.875ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> is
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{cp}=S\times {\frac {\varrho }{RT^{\text{STP}}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mi>c</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>S</mi>
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mi>ϱ<!-- ϱ --></mi>
<mrow>
<mi>R</mi>
<msup>
<mi>T</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>STP</mtext>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H^{cp}=S\times {\frac {\varrho }{RT^{\text{STP}}}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle H^{cp}=S\times {\frac {\varrho }{RT^{\text{STP}}}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5412e8b428b46e43ea69164c58cf1aa679e247bc" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:19.085ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span> ,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (March 2016)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup></dd></dl>
<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \varrho }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varrho }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\varrho" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3ef8582f3ad9ff59a6a98996548dc156de87d7c0" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.202ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is the density of the solvent, and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle T^{\text{STP}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>T</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>STP</mtext>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle T^{\text{STP}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle T^{\text{STP}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/085b38507210c8dcf249a995fd9ced532558ada5" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.172ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> = 273.15 K. The SI unit for <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle S}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>S</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="S" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is m<sup>3</sup>/kg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SazonovShaw2006_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-SazonovShaw2006-6">[6]</a></sup> The Kuenen coefficient, which is named after <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kuenen" title="Johannes Kuenen">Johannes Kuenen</a>, has been used mainly in the older literature, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IUPAC" title="IUPAC">IUPAC</a> considers it to be obsolete.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamsjäger2010_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gamsjäger2010-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p>

<h4><span id="The_Henry_volatility_defined_via_concentration_.28.7F.27.22.60UNIQ--postMath-0000004F-QINU.60.22.27.7F.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Henry_volatility_defined_via_concentration_('&quot;`UNIQ--postMath-0000004F-QINU`&quot;')">The Henry volatility defined via concentration (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle K_{\text{H}}^{pc}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<h4><span id="The_dimensionless_Henry_volatility_.7F.27.22.60UNIQ--postMath-00000055-QINU.60.22.27.7F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_dimensionless_Henry_volatility_'&quot;`UNIQ--postMath-00000055-QINU`&quot;'">The dimensionless Henry volatility <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle K_{\text{H}}^{cc}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle K_{\text{H}}^{cc}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2d5b077404f6e9a1b4caa20c2c7be47bb51ef960" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:3.75ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: The dimensionless Henry volatility  ${\displaystyle K_{\text{H}}^{cc}}">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Henry volatility can also be expressed as the dimensionless ratio between the gas-phase concentration <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c_{\text{g}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>g</mtext>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c_{\text{g}}}</annotation>
</semantics>

</p>

<p>In <a href="/wiki/Chemical_engineering" title="Chemical engineering">chemical engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_chemistry" title="Environmental chemistry">environmental chemistry</a>, this dimensionless constant is often called the <i>air–water partitioning coefficient</i> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle K_{\text{AW}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</msub>
</mstyle>

</semantics>

</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Temperature_dependence">Temperature dependence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Temperature dependence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(March 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>When the temperature of a system changes, the Henry constant also changes. The temperature dependence of equilibrium constants can generally be described with the <a href="/wiki/Van_%27t_Hoff_equation" title="Van 't Hoff equation">van 't Hoff equation</a>, which also applies to Henry's law constants:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {\mathrm {d} \ln H}{\mathrm {d} (1/T)}}={\frac {-\Delta _{\text{sol}}H}{R}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>
</mrow>
<mi>ln</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>H</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>T</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<msub>
<mi mathvariant="normal">Δ<!-- Δ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>sol</mtext>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mi>H</mi>
</mrow>
<mi>R</mi>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\frac {\mathrm {d} \ln H}{\mathrm {d} (1/T)}}={\frac {-\Delta _{\text{sol}}H}{R}},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\frac {\mathrm {d} \ln H}{\mathrm {d} (1/T)}}={\frac {-\Delta _{\text{sol}}H}{R}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d4760f679dc9157544c14312dc5494834af2a141" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:20.448ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta _{\text{sol}}H}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi mathvariant="normal">Δ<!-- Δ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>sol</mtext>
</mrow>

<p>Solubility of permanent gases usually decreases with increasing temperature at around room temperature. However, for aqueous solutions, the Henry's law solubility constant for many species goes through a minimum. For most permanent gases, the minimum is below 120 °C. Often, the smaller the gas molecule (and the lower the gas solubility in water), the lower the temperature of the maximum of the Henry's law constant. Thus, the maximum is at about 30 °C for helium, 92 to 93 °C for argon, nitrogen and oxygen, and 114 °C for xenon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Effective_Henry.27s_law_constants_Heff"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Effective_Henry's_law_constants_Heff">Effective Henry's law constants <span class="texhtml"><i>H</i><sub>eff</sub></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Effective Henry's law constants Heff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <p>The Henry's law constants mentioned so far do not consider any chemical equilibria in the aqueous phase. This type is called the "intrinsic" (or "physical") Henry's law constant. For example, the intrinsic Henry's law solubility constant of <a href="/wiki/Formaldehyde" title="Formaldehyde">formaldehyde</a> can be defined as

<p>Taking this equilibrium into account, an effective Henry's law constant <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H_{{\ce {eff}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>For acids and bases, the effective Henry's law constant is not a useful quantity because it depends on the <a href="/wiki/PH" title="PH">pH</a> of the solution.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag needs to be fact-checked with the cited source(s). (March 2016)">verification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In order to obtain a pH-independent constant, the product of the intrinsic Henry's law constant <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H^{{\ce {cp}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mstyle>

<h2><span id="Dependence_on_ionic_strength_.28Sechenov_equation.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dependence_on_ionic_strength_(Sechenov_equation)">Dependence on ionic strength (Sechenov equation)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Dependence on ionic strength (Sechenov equation)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(March 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Values of Henry's law constants for aqueous solutions depend on the composition of the solution, i.e., on its ionic strength and on dissolved organics. In general, the solubility of a gas decreases with increasing salinity ("<a href="/wiki/Salting_out" title="Salting out">salting out</a>"). However, a "<a href="/wiki/Salting_in" title="Salting in">salting in</a>" effect has also been observed, for example for the effective Henry's law constant of <a href="/wiki/Glyoxal" title="Glyoxal">glyoxal</a>. The effect can be described with the Sechenov equation, named after the Russian physiologist <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Sechenov" title="Ivan Sechenov">Ivan Sechenov</a> (sometimes the German transliteration "Setschenow" of the Cyrillic name Се́ченов is used). There are many alternative ways to define the Sechenov equation, depending on how the aqueous-phase composition is described (based on concentration, molality, or molar fraction) and which variant of the Henry's law constant is used. Describing the solution in terms of molality is preferred because molality is invariant to temperature and to the addition of dry salt to the solution. Thus, the Sechenov equation can be written as
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \log \left({\frac {H_{0}^{bp}}{H^{bp}}}\right)=k_{\text{s}}\times b({\text{salt}}),}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>

<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \log \left({\frac {H_{0}^{bp}}{H^{bp}}}\right)=k_{\text{s}}\times b({\text{salt}}),}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/be1b91c113dce5a8b079c0eeb7e4bfff67123046" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:26.471ex; height:7.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle H_{0}^{bp}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-ideal_solutions">Non-ideal solutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Henry%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Non-ideal solutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Henry's law has been shown to apply to a wide range of solutes in the limit of "infinite dilution" (<i>x</i> → 0), including non-volatile substances such as <a href="/wiki/Sucrose" title="Sucrose">sucrose</a>. In these cases, it is necessary to state the law in terms of <a href="/wiki/Chemical_potential" title="Chemical potential">chemical potentials</a>. For a solute in an ideal dilute solution, the chemical potential depends only on the concentration. For non-ideal solutions, the activity coefficients of the components must be taken into account:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mu =\mu _{c}^{\circ }+RT\ln {\frac {\gamma _{c}c}{c^{\circ }}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<msubsup>
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>c</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>∘<!-- ∘ --></mo>
</mrow>
</msubsup>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>R</mi>
<mi>T</mi>
<mi>ln</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<msub>
<mi>γ<!-- γ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>c</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mi>c</mi>
</mrow>
<msup>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>∘<!-- ∘ --></mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mu =\mu _{c}^{\circ }+RT\ln {\frac {\gamma _{c}c}{c^{\circ }}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mu =\mu _{c}^{\circ }+RT\ln {\frac {\gamma _{c}c}{c^{\circ }}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6c6352dc77eabf52f73ee54fe5dcf645b88cd25b" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:19.902ex; height:4.843ex;"/></span>,</dd></dl>
<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \gamma _{c}={\frac {K_{{\text{H}},c}}{p^{*}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</mrow>

</mrow>
</msub>

<mi>p</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</mrow>

</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>

</semantics>

</p><p>For non-ideal solutions, the <a href="/wiki/Activity_coefficient" title="Activity coefficient">activity coefficient</a> <i>γ<sub>c</sub></i> depends on the concentration and must be determined at the concentration of interest. The activity coefficient can also be obtained for non-volatile solutes, where the vapor pressure of the pure substance is negligible, by using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibbs-Duhem_relation" title="Gibbs-Duhem relation">Gibbs-Duhem relation</a>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \sum _{i}n_{i}d\mu _{i}=0.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<munder>

</mrow>
</munder>
<msub>
<mi>n</mi>

</mrow>
</msub>

<msub>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
